         <div class="fsb-clear"></div>
         <p><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-animated-02.gif"><img class="aligncenter wp-image-3074 size-full" src="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-animated-02.gif" alt="ball-tracking-animated-02" width="531" height="317"></a></p> 
         <p><em><strong>Today marks the&nbsp;100th blog post on PyImageSearch.</strong></em></p> 
         <p><strong>100 posts.&nbsp;</strong>Its hard to believe it, but its true.</p> 
         <p>When I started PyImageSearch back in January of 2014, I had no idea what the blog would turn into. I didnt know how it would evolve and mature. And I most certainly did not know how popular it would become. After 100 blog posts, I think the answer is obvious now, although I struggled to put it into words (ironic, since Im a writer)&nbsp;until I saw this tweet from&nbsp;<strong><a href="https://twitter.com/si2w" target="_blank">@si2w</a></strong>:</p> 
         <p><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/100th-post.png"><img class="aligncenter wp-image-3082" src="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/100th-post.png" alt="Big thanks for @PyImageSearch, his blog is by far the best source for projects related to OpenCV." width="600" height="215" srcset="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/100th-post.png 692w, https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/100th-post-300x108.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px"></a></p> 
         <p>I couldnt agree more. And I hope the rest of the PyImageSearch readers do as well.</p> 
         <p>Its been an incredible ride and I really have you, the PyImageSearch readers to thank. <em>Without you, this blog really wouldnt have been possible.</em></p> 
         <p>That said, to make the 100th blog post special, I thought I would do something a fun  <em>ball tracking with OpenCV:</em></p> 
         <p><iframe width="500" height="375" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/dKpRsdYSCLQ?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
         <p>The goal here is fair self-explanatory:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><strong>Step #1:&nbsp;</strong>Detect the presence of a&nbsp;colored ball using computer vision techniques.</li> 
          <li><strong>Step #2:&nbsp;</strong>Track the ball as it moves around in the video frames, drawing its previous positions as it moves.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>The end product should look similar to the GIF and video&nbsp;above.</p> 
         <p>After reading this blog post, youll have a good idea on how to track balls (and other objects) in video streams using Python and OpenCV.</p> 
         <div style="padding-top: 10px; padding-bottom: 15px; padding-right: 10px; height: 70px; background: url('https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/download-code-icon.png'); background-size: 70px 70px; background-repeat: no-repeat;"> 
          <p style="margin-top: 1px; margin-left: 80px; font-weight: bold;">Looking for the source code to this post?<br> <a id="scroll_to_code" href="#">Jump right to the downloads section.</a></p> 
         </div> 
         <h2>Ball tracking with OpenCV</h2> 
         <p>Lets get this example started. Open up a new file, name it <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb54c797581876" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">ball_tracking</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">py</span></span></span>&nbsp;, and well get coding:</p>

from collections import deque
import numpy as np
import argparse
import imutils
import cv2

# construct the argument parse and parse the arguments
ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
ap.add_argument("-v", "--video",
	help="path to the (optional) video file")
ap.add_argument("-b", "--buffer", type=int, default=64,
	help="max buffer size")
args = vars(ap.parse_args())</textarea>

         </div> 
         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0024 seconds] --> 
         <p><strong>Lines 2-6</strong> handle importing our necessary packages. Well be using <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb55d173915330" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">deque</span></span></span>&nbsp;, a <a href="https://docs.python.org/2/library/collections.html#collections.deque" target="_blank">list-like data structure</a> with super fast appends and pops to maintain a list of the past&nbsp;<em>N</em>&nbsp;<em>(x, y)</em>-locations of the ball in our video stream. Maintaining such a queue allows us to draw the contrail of the ball as its being tracked.</p> 
         <p>Well also be using <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb561904725226" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">imutils</span></span></span>&nbsp;, my collection of OpenCV&nbsp;convenience functions to make a few basic tasks (like resizing) much easier. If you dont already have <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb564459505480" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">imutils</span></span></span>&nbsp; installed on your system, you can <a href="https://github.com/jrosebr1/imutils" target="_blank">grab the source from GitHub</a> or just use <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb567858193257" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">pip</span></span></span>&nbsp; to install it:</p>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] --> 
         <p>From there,&nbsp;<strong>Lines 9-14</strong> handle parsing our command line arguments. The first switch, <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb56c930021765" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">video</span></span></span>&nbsp; is the (optional) path to our example video file. If this switch&nbsp;<em>is supplied</em>, then OpenCV will grab a pointer to the video file and read frames from it. Otherwise, if this switch <i>is not supplied</i>, then OpenCV will try to access our webcam.</p> 
         <p>If this your first time running this script,&nbsp;<strong>I suggest using the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb56e733413782" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">video</span></span></span>&nbsp; switch to start:</strong>&nbsp;this will demonstrate the functionality of the Python script to you, then you can modify the script, video file, and webcam access to your liking.</p> 
         <p>A second optional argument, <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb571858804523" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">buffer</span></span></span>&nbsp; is the maximum size of our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb573445154705" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">deque</span></span></span>&nbsp;, which maintains a list of the previous&nbsp;<em>(x, y)-</em>coordinates of the ball we are tracking. This <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb575969078315" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">deque</span></span></span>&nbsp; allows us to draw the contrail of the ball, detailing its past locations. A smaller queue will lead to a shorter tail whereas a larger queue will create a longer tail (since more points are being tracked):</p> 
         <div id="attachment_3076" style="width: 610px" class="wp-caption aligncenter">
          <a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-tails-comparison.jpg"><img class="wp-image-3076" src="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-tails-comparison.jpg" alt="Figure 1: An example of a short contrail&nbsp;(buffer=32) on the left, and a longer contrail&nbsp;(buffer=128) on the right. Notice that as the size of the buffer increases, so does the length of the contrail." width="600" height="197" srcset="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-tails-comparison.jpg 1000w, https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-tails-comparison-300x99.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px"></a>
          <p class="wp-caption-text"><strong>Figure 1:</strong> An example of a short contrail&nbsp;(<em>buffer=32</em>) on the <em>left</em>, and a longer contrail&nbsp;(<em>buffer=128</em>) on the <em>right</em>. Notice that as the size of the buffer increases, so does the length of the contrail.</p>
         </div>

           <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
# import the necessary packages
from collections import deque
import numpy as np
import argparse
import imutils
import cv2

# construct the argument parse and parse the arguments
ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
ap.add_argument("-v", "--video",
	help="path to the (optional) video file")
ap.add_argument("-b", "--buffer", type=int, default=64,
	help="max buffer size")
args = vars(ap.parse_args())

# define the lower and upper boundaries of the "green"
# ball in the HSV color space, then initialize the
# list of tracked points
greenLower = (29, 86, 6)
greenUpper = (64, 255, 255)
pts = deque(maxlen=args["buffer"])

# if a video path was not supplied, grab the reference
# to the webcam
if not args.get("video", False):
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

# otherwise, grab a reference to the video file
else:
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(args["video"])</textarea>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0089 seconds] --> 
         <p><strong>Lines 19 and 20</strong> define the lower and upper boundaries of the color&nbsp;<em>green</em> in the HSV color space (which I determined using the <a href="https://github.com/jrosebr1/imutils/blob/master/bin/range-detector" target="_blank">range-detector</a> script in the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb57c439471316" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">imutils</span></span></span>&nbsp; library). These color boundaries will allow us to detect the green ball in our video file.&nbsp;<strong>Line 21</strong>&nbsp;then initializes our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb57f161035465" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">deque</span></span></span>&nbsp; of <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb581095139954" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">pts</span></span></span>&nbsp; using the supplied maximum buffer size (which defaults to <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb584273190891" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-cn">64</span></span></span>&nbsp;).</p> 
         <p>From there, we need to grab access to our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb586550238066" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">camera</span></span></span>&nbsp; pointer. If a <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb589817416237" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">video</span></span></span>&nbsp; switch was&nbsp;<em>not supplied</em>, then we grab reference to our webcam (<strong>Lines 25 and 26</strong>). Otherwise, if a video file path&nbsp;<em>was supplied</em>, then we open it for reading and grab a reference pointer on&nbsp;<strong>Lines 29 and 30</strong>.</p>

           <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
# import the necessary packages
from collections import deque
import numpy as np
import argparse
import imutils
import cv2

# construct the argument parse and parse the arguments
ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
ap.add_argument("-v", "--video",
	help="path to the (optional) video file")
ap.add_argument("-b", "--buffer", type=int, default=64,
	help="max buffer size")
args = vars(ap.parse_args())

# define the lower and upper boundaries of the "green"
# ball in the HSV color space, then initialize the
# list of tracked points
greenLower = (29, 86, 6)
greenUpper = (64, 255, 255)
pts = deque(maxlen=args["buffer"])

# if a video path was not supplied, grab the reference
# to the webcam
if not args.get("video", False):
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

# otherwise, grab a reference to the video file
else:
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(args["video"])

# keep looping
while True:
	# grab the current frame
	(grabbed, frame) = camera.read()

	# if we are viewing a video and we did not grab a frame,
	# then we have reached the end of the video
	if args.get("video") and not grabbed:
		break

	# resize the frame, blur it, and convert it to the HSV
	# color space
	frame = imutils.resize(frame, width=600)
	# blurred = cv2.GaussianBlur(frame, (11, 11), 0)
	hsv = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2HSV)

	# construct a mask for the color "green", then perform
	# a series of dilations and erosions to remove any small
	# blobs left in the mask
	mask = cv2.inRange(hsv, greenLower, greenUpper)
	mask = cv2.erode(mask, None, iterations=2)
	mask = cv2.dilate(mask, None, iterations=2)</textarea>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0148 seconds] --> 
         <p><strong>Line 33</strong> starts a loop that will continue until (1) we press the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb58f672096357" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">q</span></span></span>&nbsp; key, indicating that we want to terminate the script or (2) our video file reaches its end and runs out of frames.</p> 
         <p><strong>Line 35</strong>&nbsp;makes a call to the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb592647719107" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">read</span></span></span>&nbsp; method of our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb595077386370" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">camera</span></span></span>&nbsp; pointer which returns a 2-tuple. The first entry in the tuple, <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb597405634976" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">grabbed</span></span></span>&nbsp; is a boolean indicating whether the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb59a699798704" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; was successfully read or not. The <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb59c827775127" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; is the video&nbsp;frame itself.</p> 
         <p>In the case we are reading from a video file and the frame is not successfully read, then we know we are at the end of the video and can break from the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb59f981120439" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-st">while</span></span></span>&nbsp; loop (<strong>Lines 39 and 40</strong>).</p> 
         <p><strong>Lines 44-46</strong> preprocess our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5a1533537692" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; a bit. First, we resize the frame to have a width of&nbsp;<em>600px</em>. Downsizing the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5a4284228128" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; allows us to process the frame faster, leading to an <i>increase</i> in FPS (since we have less image data to process). Well then blur the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5a6318248821" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; to reduce high frequency noise and allow us to focus on the structural objects inside the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5a9856822212" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp;, such as the ball. Finally, well convert the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ab201451395" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; to the HSV color space.</p> 
         <p><strong>Lines 51&nbsp;</strong>handles the actual&nbsp;<em>localization</em>&nbsp;of the green ball in the frame by making a call to <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ad082227745" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">cv2</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">inRange</span></span></span>&nbsp;. We first supply the lower HSV color boundaries for the color&nbsp;<em>green</em>, followed by the upper HSV boundaries. The output of <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b0183080082" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">cv2</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">inRange</span></span></span>&nbsp; is a binary <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b2185547640" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">mask</span></span></span>&nbsp;, like this one:</p> 
         <div id="attachment_3077" style="width: 610px" class="wp-caption aligncenter">
          <a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-mask.jpg"><img class="wp-image-3077" src="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-mask.jpg" alt="Figure 2: Generating a mask for the green ball using the cv2.inRange function." width="600" height="214" srcset="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-mask.jpg 1000w, https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-mask-300x107.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px"></a>
          <p class="wp-caption-text"><strong>Figure 2:</strong> Generating a mask for the green ball using the cv2.inRange function.</p>
         </div> 
         <p>As we can see, we have successfully detected the green ball in the image.&nbsp;A series of erosions and dilations (<strong>Lines 52 and 53</strong>) remove any small blobs that my be left on the mask.</p> 
         <p>Alright, time to perform compute the contour (i.e. outline) of the green ball and draw it on our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b5791832274" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp;:</p>
         <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta --> 
         <div id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"> 
          <div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" show" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
           <span class="crayon-title">Ball Tracking with OpenCV</span>

          <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
           <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
# import the necessary packages
from collections import deque
import numpy as np
import argparse
import imutils
import cv2

# construct the argument parse and parse the arguments
ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
ap.add_argument("-v", "--video",
	help="path to the (optional) video file")
ap.add_argument("-b", "--buffer", type=int, default=64,
	help="max buffer size")
args = vars(ap.parse_args())

# define the lower and upper boundaries of the "green"
# ball in the HSV color space, then initialize the
# list of tracked points
greenLower = (29, 86, 6)
greenUpper = (64, 255, 255)
pts = deque(maxlen=args["buffer"])

# if a video path was not supplied, grab the reference
# to the webcam
if not args.get("video", False):
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

# otherwise, grab a reference to the video file
else:
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(args["video"])

# keep looping
while True:
	# grab the current frame
	(grabbed, frame) = camera.read()

	# if we are viewing a video and we did not grab a frame,
	# then we have reached the end of the video
	if args.get("video") and not grabbed:
		break

	# resize the frame, blur it, and convert it to the HSV
	# color space
	frame = imutils.resize(frame, width=600)
	# blurred = cv2.GaussianBlur(frame, (11, 11), 0)
	hsv = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2HSV)

	# construct a mask for the color "green", then perform
	# a series of dilations and erosions to remove any small
	# blobs left in the mask
	mask = cv2.inRange(hsv, greenLower, greenUpper)
	mask = cv2.erode(mask, None, iterations=2)
	mask = cv2.dilate(mask, None, iterations=2)

	# find contours in the mask and initialize the current
	# (x, y) center of the ball
	cnts = cv2.findContours(mask.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL,
		cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)[-2]
	center = None

	# only proceed if at least one contour was found
	if len(cnts) &gt; 0:
		# find the largest contour in the mask, then use
		# it to compute the minimum enclosing circle and
		# centroid
		c = max(cnts, key=cv2.contourArea)
		((x, y), radius) = cv2.minEnclosingCircle(c)
		M = cv2.moments(c)
		center = (int(M["m10"] / M["m00"]), int(M["m01"] / M["m00"]))

		# only proceed if the radius meets a minimum size
		if radius &gt; 10:
			# draw the circle and centroid on the frame,
			# then update the list of tracked points
			cv2.circle(frame, (int(x), int(y)), int(radius),
				(0, 255, 255), 2)
			cv2.circle(frame, center, 5, (0, 0, 255), -1)

	# update the points queue
	pts.appendleft(center)</textarea>
          </div>

              <td class="crayon-code">
               <div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-55">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-c"># find contours in the mask and initialize the current</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-56">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-c"># (x, y) center of the ball</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-57">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cnts</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">=</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cv2</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">.</span>
                 <span class="crayon-e">findContours</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">(</span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">mask</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">.</span>
                 <span class="crayon-k ">copy</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">(</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">)</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">,</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cv2</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">.</span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">RETR_EXTERNAL</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">,</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-58">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cv2</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">.</span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">)</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">[</span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">-</span>
                 <span class="crayon-cn">2</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">]</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-59">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">center</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">=</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-t">None</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-60">
                 &nbsp;
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-61">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-c"># only proceed if at least one contour was found</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-62">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-st">if</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-k ">len</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">(</span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cnts</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">)</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">&gt;</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-cn">0</span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">:</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-63">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-c"># find the largest contour in the mask, then use</span>
                </div>
                <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5b8139402454-64">
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>

                 <span class="crayon-o">=</span>

                 <span class="crayon-k ">max</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">(</span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">cnts</span>
                 <span class="crayon-sy">,</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">key</span>

                 <span class="crayon-sy">(</span>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0144 seconds] --> 
         <p>We start by computing the contours of the object(s) in the image on&nbsp;<strong>Line 57</strong>. We specify an array slice of&nbsp;<em>-2</em> to make the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5bc066028384" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">cv2</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">findContours</span></span></span>&nbsp; function compatible with&nbsp;<strong><em>both</em></strong> OpenCV 2.4 and OpenCV 3. You can read more about why this change to <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5c0701716361" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">cv2</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">findContours</span></span></span>&nbsp; is necessary in <a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/08/10/checking-your-opencv-version-using-python/" target="_blank">this blog post</a>. Well also initialize the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5c2583929575" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">center</span></span></span>&nbsp; <em>(x, y)</em>-coordinates of the ball to <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5c5739492441" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">None</span></span></span>&nbsp; on&nbsp;<strong>Line 59</strong>.</p> 
         <p><strong>Line 62</strong> makes a check to ensure&nbsp;<em>at least one</em> contour was found in the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5c7355408254" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">mask</span></span></span>&nbsp;. Provided that at least one contour was found, we find the largest contour in the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5c9735703928" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">cnts</span></span></span>&nbsp; list on&nbsp;<strong>Line 66</strong>, compute the minimum enclosing circle of the blob, and then compute the center&nbsp;<em>(x, y)</em>-coordinates (i.e. the centroids) on&nbsp;<strong>Lines 68 and 69</strong>.</p> 
         <p><strong>Line 72</strong>&nbsp;makes a quick check to ensure that the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5cc622483850" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">radius</span></span></span>&nbsp; of the minimum enclosing circle is sufficiently large. Provided that the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ce986467454" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">radius</span></span></span>&nbsp; passes the test, we then draw two circles: one surrounding the ball itself and another to indicate the centroid of the ball.</p> 
         <p>Finally,&nbsp;<strong>Line 80</strong> appends the centroid to the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5d1278496020" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">pts</span></span></span>&nbsp; list.</p> 
         <p>The last step is to draw the&nbsp;contrail of the ball, or simply the past&nbsp;<em>N</em>&nbsp;<em>(x, y)</em>-coordinates the ball has been detected at. This is also a straightforward process:</p>
         <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta --> 
         <div id="crayon-59d374cfeb5d4977415452" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"> 
          <div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" show" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
           <span class="crayon-title">Ball Tracking with OpenCV</span> 
           <div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
            <div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers">

          <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
           <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
# import the necessary packages
from collections import deque
import numpy as np
import argparse
import imutils
import cv2

# construct the argument parse and parse the arguments
ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
ap.add_argument("-v", "--video",
	help="path to the (optional) video file")
ap.add_argument("-b", "--buffer", type=int, default=64,
	help="max buffer size")
args = vars(ap.parse_args())

# define the lower and upper boundaries of the "green"
# ball in the HSV color space, then initialize the
# list of tracked points
greenLower = (29, 86, 6)
greenUpper = (64, 255, 255)
pts = deque(maxlen=args["buffer"])

# if a video path was not supplied, grab the reference
# to the webcam
if not args.get("video", False):
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(0)

# otherwise, grab a reference to the video file
else:
	camera = cv2.VideoCapture(args["video"])

# keep looping
while True:
	# grab the current frame
	(grabbed, frame) = camera.read()

	# if we are viewing a video and we did not grab a frame,
	# then we have reached the end of the video
	if args.get("video") and not grabbed:
		break

	# resize the frame, blur it, and convert it to the HSV
	# color space
	frame = imutils.resize(frame, width=600)
	# blurred = cv2.GaussianBlur(frame, (11, 11), 0)
	hsv = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2HSV)

	# construct a mask for the color "green", then perform
	# a series of dilations and erosions to remove any small
	# blobs left in the mask
	mask = cv2.inRange(hsv, greenLower, greenUpper)
	mask = cv2.erode(mask, None, iterations=2)
	mask = cv2.dilate(mask, None, iterations=2)

	# find contours in the mask and initialize the current
	# (x, y) center of the ball
	cnts = cv2.findContours(mask.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL,
		cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)[-2]
	center = None

	# only proceed if at least one contour was found
	if len(cnts) &gt; 0:
		# find the largest contour in the mask, then use
		# it to compute the minimum enclosing circle and
		# centroid
		c = max(cnts, key=cv2.contourArea)
		((x, y), radius) = cv2.minEnclosingCircle(c)
		M = cv2.moments(c)
		center = (int(M["m10"] / M["m00"]), int(M["m01"] / M["m00"]))

		# only proceed if the radius meets a minimum size
		if radius &gt; 10:
			# draw the circle and centroid on the frame,
			# then update the list of tracked points
			cv2.circle(frame, (int(x), int(y)), int(radius),
				(0, 255, 255), 2)
			cv2.circle(frame, center, 5, (0, 0, 255), -1)

	# update the points queue
	pts.appendleft(center)

	# loop over the set of tracked points
	for i in xrange(1, len(pts)):
		# if either of the tracked points are None, ignore
		# them
		if pts[i - 1] is None or pts[i] is None:
			continue

		# otherwise, compute the thickness of the line and
		# draw the connecting lines
		thickness = int(np.sqrt(args["buffer"] / float(i + 1)) * 2.5)
		cv2.line(frame, pts[i - 1], pts[i], (0, 0, 255), thickness)

	# show the frame to our screen
	cv2.imshow("Frame", frame)
	key = cv2.waitKey(1) &amp; 0xFF

	# if the 'q' key is pressed, stop the loop
	if key == ord("q"):
		break

# cleanup the camera and close any open windows
camera.release()
cv2.destroyAllWindows()</textarea>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0321 seconds] --> 
         <p>We start looping over each of the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5d9484997960" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">pts</span></span></span>&nbsp; on&nbsp;<strong>Line 84</strong>. If either the current point or the previous point is <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5dc685576520" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">None</span></span></span>&nbsp; (indicating that the ball was not successfully detected in that given frame), then we ignore the current index continue looping over the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5df416134663" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">pts</span></span></span>&nbsp; (<strong>Lines 86 and 87</strong>).</p> 
         <p>Provided that both points are valid, we compute the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5e1659125816" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">thickness</span></span></span>&nbsp; of the contrail and then draw it on the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5e3077237136" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; (<strong>Lines 91 and 92</strong>).</p> 
         <p>The remainder of our <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5e6663894386" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">ball_tracking</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">py</span></span></span>&nbsp; script simply performs some basic housekeeping by displaying the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5e8465068010" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">frame</span></span></span>&nbsp; to our screen, detecting any key presses, and then releasing the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ea190081826" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">camera</span></span></span>&nbsp; pointer.</p> 
         <h2>Ball tracking in action</h2> 
         <p>Now that our script has been coded it up, lets give it a try. Open up a terminal and execute the following command:</p>

                <div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-59d374cfeb5ed412091316-1">
                 1
                </div>
               </div> </td> 
              <td class="crayon-code">
               <div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">
                <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ed412091316-1">
                 <span class="crayon-sy">$</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-e">python </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">ball_tracking</span>
                 <span class="crayon-e">.py</span>
                 <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                 <span class="crayon-o">--</span>
                 <span class="crayon-e">video </span>
                 <span class="crayon-v">ball_tracking_example</span>
                 <span class="crayon-e">.mp4</span>
                </div>
               </div></td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody>
           </table> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] --> 
         <p>This command will kick off our script using the supplied <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5ef494272114" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-v">ball_tracking_example</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-v">mp4</span></span></span>&nbsp; demo video. Below you can find a few animated GIFs of the successful ball detection and tracking using OpenCV:</p> 
         <div id="attachment_3078" style="width: 546px" class="wp-caption aligncenter">
          <a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-animated-01.gif"><img class="size-full wp-image-3078" src="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/ball-tracking-animated-01.gif" alt="Figure 3: An example of successfully performing ball tracking with OpenCV." width="536" height="316"></a>

         <p>Finally, if you want to execute the script using your webcam rather than the supplied video file, simply omit the <span id="crayon-59d374cfeb5f2281910975" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-o">--</span><span class="crayon-v">video</span></span></span>&nbsp; switch:</p>

         <!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] --> 
         <p>However, to see any results, you will need a green object with the same HSV color range was the one I used in this demo.</p> 
         <h2>Summary</h2> 
         <p>In this blog post we learned how to perform ball tracking with OpenCV. The Python script we developed was able to (1) <em>detect the presence of the colored ball</em>, followed by (2) <em>track and draw&nbsp;the position of the ball</em> as it moved around the screen.</p> 
         <p>As the results showed, our system was quite robust and able to track the ball even if it was partially occluded from view by my hand.</p> 
         <p>Our script&nbsp;was also able to operate at an extremely high frame rate (<i>&gt; 32&nbsp;</i>FPS), indicating that color based tracking methods are very much suitable for real-time detection and tracking.</p> 
         <p>If you enjoyed this blog post, please consider subscribing to the PyImageSearch Newsletter by entering your email address in the form below  this blog (<em>and the 99 posts preceding it</em>) wouldnt be possible without readers like yourself.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-358801"> 
              <p>Great question Andrew, thanks for asking. If you had more than 1 ball in the image, you would simply loop over each of the contours individually, make sure they are of sufficient size, and draw their enclosing circles individually. And if you wanted to track multiple balls of different <em>colors</em>, you would need to define a list of lower and upper boundaries, loop over them, and then create a mask for each set of boundaries.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-358808"> 
              <p>Tracking fast moving objects in sports such as tennis balls and hockey pucks is a deceptively challenging problem. The issues arrises from the objects moving <em>so fast</em> that the standard computer vision algorithms cant really process them  all they see is a bunch of motion blur. Im not sure about tennis, but I know in the case of hockey they ended up putting a chip in the puck that interfaces with other algorithms, allowing it to be more easier tracked (and thus watched on TV).</p>

               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=358808#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-358808&quot;, &quot;358808&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 16, 2015 at 7:26 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-359245" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-359245"> 
              <p>Unfortunately, using VirtualBox you will not be able to access the raw webcam stream from your OSX machine. This is considered to be a security concern. Imagine if a VM could access your webcam anytime it wanted! So, because of this, accessing the raw webcam is disabled. In this case, you have two options:</p> 
              <p>1. Try <a target="blank" href="http://www.vmware.com/" rel="nofollow">VMWare</a> which does allow for the webcam to be accessed from the VM. I personally have not tried this out, but I have heard this from other.<br> 2. Install OpenCV on your native OSX machine.</p> 
              <p>I hope that helps!</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=359245#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-359245&quot;, &quot;359245&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-359600"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-359600" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 17, 2015 at 8:15 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-359600" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-359600"> 
              <p>Any time you see an error related to an image being <code>None</code> and not having a <code>shape</code> attribute, its because the image/frame was either (1) not loaded from disk, indicating that the path to the image is incorrect, or (2) a frame is not being read properly from your video stream. Based on your provided command, it looks like you are trying to access the webcam of your system. Try using the supplied video (in the code download of this post) and see if it works. If it does, then the issue is with your webcam.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=359600#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-359600&quot;, &quot;359600&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

                   <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-424006"> 
                    <p>That really depends on the types of digits youre trying to detect as well as the environment they are in. Typical methods for object detection in general include <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">Histogram of Oriented Gradients</a>. I cover object detection in detail inside the <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/pyimagesearch-gurus/">PyImageSearch Gurus course</a>, but without seeing an example image of what youre trying to detect, I cant point you in the right direction.</p>

           <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-359578"> 
            <p>Hi,</p> 
            <p>Just figured it out.<br> To use this code on a Raspberry Pi with Python3 OpenCV3 and the RaspiCAM I needed to load the v4l2 driver:</p> 
            <p>sudo modprobe bcm2835-v4l2</p> 
            <p>To load the driver every time the RPi boots up, just add the following line to /etc/modules </p> 
            <p>bcm2835.v4l2</p> 
            <p>Thanks for the tutorial</p> 
            <div class="reply"> 
             <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=359578#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-359578&quot;, &quot;359578&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Luis">Reply</a>

             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-360063"> 
              <p>When the HSV drops out of the frame, the HSV boundaries are simply used to pick it back up when it re-enters the scene. To answer your second question, since this is a basic demonstration of how to perform object detection, Im only using color-based methods. In future methods Ill show more robust approaches using features.</p>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-365344"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-365344" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">October 2, 2015 at 7:10 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-365344" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-365344"> 
              <p>Hey Ali  great questions, thanks for asking. If the ball is black, that could cause some issues when using color based detection, but thats actually not too much of an issue provided that there is enough contrast between the black color and the rest of the image scene. Whats actually really concerning is the very high speed of the ball. Motion blur can really, <em>really</em> hurt the performance of computer vision algorithms. I think you would need a very high FPS camera, incorporate color tracking (if at all possible), and might want to use a bit of <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/" rel="nofollow">machine learning</a> to build a custom squash ball tracker.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=365344#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-365344&quot;, &quot;365344&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

            <p>Hi Adrian,</p> 
            <p>When there is initially no contour in the mask, and then the green object is moved into view, it will generate a deque index out of range exception on line 94.</p> 
            <p>I Modified line 94 to:</p> 
            <p>if counter &gt;= 10 and i == 1 and len(pts) &gt;= 10 and pts[-10] is not None:</p> 
            <p>That seems to have solved it.</p> 
            <p>Thank you very much for sharing your image-processing knowledge, I learned some neat tricks from it and I hope you will be keeping up this good work.</p> 
            <p>Cheers,<br> Willem.</p>

           <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-384697"> 
            <p>Hello,<br> I tried to run this but its giving me this error: </p> 
            <p></p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-385656"> 
              <p>All you really need are some <code>if</code> statements and the bounding box of the contour. For example, if I wanted to see if the ball entered the top-left corner of my frame, I would do something like:</p> 
              <p></p>
              <!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta --> 
              <div id="crayon-59d374d018453566096162" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"> 
               <div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" show" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
                <span class="crayon-title"></span> 
                <div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;">
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window">
                  <div class="crayon-button-icon"></div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div> 
               <div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div> 
               <div class="crayon-plain-wrap">
                <textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
if x &lt;= 50 and y &lt;= 50:
    # do something</textarea>
               </div> 
               <div class="crayon-main" style=""> 
                <table class="crayon-table"> 
                 <tbody>
                  <tr class="crayon-row"> 
                   <td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show"> 
                    <div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
                     <div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-59d374d018453566096162-1">
                      1
                     </div>
                     <div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-59d374d018453566096162-2">
                      2
                     </div>
                    </div> </td> 
                   <td class="crayon-code">
                    <div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;">
                     <div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-59d374d018453566096162-1">
                      <span class="crayon-st">if</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-v">x</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-o">&lt;=</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-cn">50</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-st">and</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-v">y</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-o">&lt;=</span>
                      <span class="crayon-h"> </span>
                      <span class="crayon-cn">50</span>
                      <span class="crayon-o">:</span>
                     </div>
                     <div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-59d374d018453566096162-2">
                      <span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>
                      <span class="crayon-p"># do something</span>
                     </div>
                    </div></td>

                 </tbody>
                </table> 
               </div>

              <!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] --> 
              <p></p> 
              <p>The code in the <code>if</code> statement will only fire if the center of the ball is within the upper-left corner of the frame (within 50 pixels). You can of course modify the code to suit your needs.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-389001"> 
              <p>Any time you see an image or frame being NoneType its almost 100% due to the fact that (1) the image is not correctly read from disk or (2) the frame could not be read from the video stream. I would double check that you can properly access your webcam via OpenCV since that is likely were the issue lies.</p>

              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">February 5, 2016 at 9:17 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-389147" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-389147"> 
              <p>This is used to take the <a target="blank" href="https://wiki.python.org/moin/BitwiseOperators" rel="nofollow">bitwise AND</a> between the return value of <code>cv2.waitKey</code> gives the least significant byte. This byte is then passed into the <code>ord</code> function so we can get the actual value of the key press.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=389147#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-389147&quot;, &quot;389147&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <span class="edit"></span>

             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-389474"> 
              <p>To transform the RGB values to HSV values, its best to use the <code>cv2.cvtColor</code> function. You can find the formula for the conversion on <a target="blank" href="http://docs.opencv.org/2.4/modules/imgproc/doc/miscellaneous_transformations.html#cvtcolor" rel="nofollow">this page</a>. However, if youre trying to detect a different color object, I suggest using the <code>range-detector</code> script I mention in this post.</p>

               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=389474#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-389474&quot;, &quot;389474&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-390320"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-390320" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">February 16, 2016 at 3:36 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-390320" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-390320"> 
              <p>Anytime you see a <code>NoneType</code> error its 99% of the time due to an image not being read properly from disk or a frame not being read from the video stream. The issue here is that youre using <code>cv2.VideoCapture</code> when you should instead be using the <code>picamera</code> Python package to access the Raspberry Pi camera module. You can read more on how to <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/03/30/accessing-the-raspberry-pi-camera-with-opencv-and-python/" rel="nofollow">access the Raspberry Pi camera module here</a>. </p> 
              <p>You could also swap out the <code>cv2.VideoCapture</code> for the <code>VideoStream</code> that works with <em>both</em> the Raspberry Pi camera module and USB webcams. <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2016/01/04/unifying-picamera-and-cv2-videocapture-into-a-single-class-with-opencv/" rel="nofollow">Find out more here</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=390320#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-390320&quot;, &quot;390320&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

                 <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-390665"> 
                  <p>Thats definitely a bit more of a challenge. To start, <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/09/29/finding-brightest-spot-image-using-python-opencv/" rel="nofollow">youll want to find the brightest spots in an image</a>. Then, youll need to filter these regions and apply a heuristic of some sort. A first try would be finding two spots in an image that are lie approximately on the same horizontal line. You might also want to try <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/" rel="nofollow">training an object detector</a> to detect the front of the car prior to processing the ROI for headlights.</p>

                    <p>The same code can be applied. Just define the color ranges for each object you want to detect, then create a mask for each of the color ranges.                    <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                   <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-392611"> 
                    <p>The most important aspect of getting <em>multiple</em> colors is to use <em>multiple</em> masks  one for each color you want to track. You then apply each technique of color thresholding, finding the largest contour(s), and then tracking then. But again, you need to create a mask for <em>each</em> color range that you want to track.</p>
