           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-390437"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-390437" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">February 18, 2016 at 9:30 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-390437" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-390437"> 
              <p>So keep in mind that the <code>FPS</code> is <em>not measuring the physical FPS of your camera sensor</em>. Instead, <em><strong>its measuring the total number of frames you can process in a single second</strong></em>. The more steps you add to your video processing pipeline, the slower it will run.</p> 
              <p>Your results reflect this as well. When using just <code>cv2.imshow</code> you were able to process 39 frames per second. However, once you included smoothing, color thresholding, and contour detection, your processing rate dropped to 7 frames per second. Again, this makes sense  you are adding more steps to your processing pipeline, therefore you cannot process as many frames per second.</p> 
              <p>Think of your video processing pipeline as a flight of stairs. The less functions you have to call inside your pipeline (i.e., the while loop), the faster you can go down the stairs. The more functions you have, the longer your staircase becomes  and therefore it takes longer for you to descend the stairs.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=390437#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-390437&quot;, &quot;390437&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

                 <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-408382"> 
                  <p>There are many ways to execute the <code>range-detector</code> script but most are based on how your Python PATH is defined. Where do you have the <code>imutils</code> package installed on your system? The script itself is already in <code>imutils</code>. The easiest method would be to change directory to it and execute using your input image/video stream as the source.</p>

              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-392811"> 
              <p>I would recommend against this. Trying to detect and recognize objects that are reflective is very challenging due to the fact that reflective materials (by definition) reflect light back into the camera. Thus, it becomes very hard to define a color range for reflective materials. Instead, if at all possible, change the color of the object you are tracking.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=392811#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-392811&quot;, &quot;392811&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

                 <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                 <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-393036"> 
                  <p>If the contours are overlapping, then that will cause an issue with the tracking  this is also why you might want to consider using different color objects for tracking. In the case of overlapping objects, you should consider applying <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/11/02/watershed-opencv/" rel="nofollow">the watershed algorithm</a> for segmentation.</p>

                   <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=393036#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-393036&quot;, &quot;393036&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-2"> <a name="comment-394135"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-394135" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">April 6, 2016 at 9:08 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-394135" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-394135"> 
              <p>There are many ways to accomplish this, some easy, some complicated. The quickest solution is to compute the centroid of each object in the frame. Then, find the objects in the next frame. Compute the centroids again. Take the Euclidean distance between the centroids. The pairs of objects that have the smallest distances are thus the same object. This would make for a great blog post in the future, so Ill make sure I cover that.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=394135#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-394135&quot;, &quot;394135&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

                 <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-5"> <a name="comment-394996"></a> 
                  <div id="li-comment-394996" class="comment-container"> 
                   <div class="avatar">
                    <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
                   </div> 
                   <div class="comment-head"> 
                    <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
                    <span class="date">April 15, 2016 at 12:11 pm</span> 
                    <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-394996" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
                    <span class="edit"></span> 
                   </div>
                   <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                   <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-394996"> 
                    <p>The (x, y)-coordinates of the ball are obtained from the image itself. They are found by thresholding the image, finding the contour corresponding to the ball, and then computing its center. These coordinates are then stored in a queue (i.e., the actual tracking part). If you would like to add in tracking along the z-axis, youll need to see the blog post I linked you to above. The trick is apply an initial calibration step that can be used to measure the perceived distance in pixels and convert the pixels to actual measurable units.</p> 
                    <div class="reply"> 
                    </div>
                    <!-- /.reply --> 
                   </div>
                   <!-- /comment-entry --> 
                  </div>

                   <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                   <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-395284"> 
                    <p>For 3D tracking, youll likely want to explore other avenues. If you want to use a 2D camera (which would be a bit challenging), then camera calibration via intrinsic parameters would be required. Otherwise, you might want to look into stereo/depth cameras for more advanced tracking methods. Hopefully Ill be able to cover both of these techniques in future blog posts ?</p> 
                    <div class="reply"> 
                    </div>
                    <!-- /.reply --> 
                   </div>
                   <!-- /comment-entry --> 
                  </div>

             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">April 14, 2016 at 4:36 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-394937" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-394937"> 
              <p>The <code>cv2.minEnclosingCircle</code> does indeed return the center (x, y)-coordinates of the circle. However, it presumes that the shape is a perfect circle (which is not always the case during the segmentation). So instead, you can compute the moments of the object and obtain a weighted center. This is a more accurate representation of the center coordinates.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=394937#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-394937&quot;, &quot;394937&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-395843"></a>

             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">April 25, 2016 at 2:09 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-395843" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-395843"> 
              <p>It sounds like youre using OpenCV 3; however, this blog post utilizes OpenCV 2.4. To fix this error, you simply need to change the <code>cv2.findContours</code> line to:</p> 
              <p><code>(_, cnts, _) = cv2.findContours(mask.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL, cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)</code></p> 
              <p>I detail the difference in <code>cv2.findContours</code> between OpenCV 2.4 and OpenCV 3 in <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/08/10/checking-your-opencv-version-using-python/" rel="nofollow">this blog post</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=395843#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-395843&quot;, &quot;395843&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

                  <span class="edit"></span> 
                 </div>
                 <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                 <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-395896"> 
                  <p>My mistake  I read your original comment to fast. I should have been able to tell that you were using OpenCV 2.4. In that case, you just need to modify the code to be:</p> 
                  <p><code>(cnts, _) = cv2.findContours(mask.copy(), cv2.RETR_EXTERNAL, cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)</code></p> 
                  <p>I discuss the changes in the <code>cv2.findContours</code> function between OpenCV 2.4 and OpenCV 3 <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/08/10/checking-your-opencv-version-using-python/" rel="nofollow">in this blog post</a>.</p> 
                  <div class="reply"> 
                   <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=395896#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-395896&quot;, &quot;395896&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
                  </div>

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">April 25, 2016 at 1:59 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-395832" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-395832"> 
              <p>I wouldnt recommend using Hough Circles for this. Not only are the parameters a bit tricky to get just right, but the other issue is at high speeds, the ball will become motion blurred and not really resemble a circle. Instead, I would suggest using a simple contour method like I detailed in this blog post. Otherwise, if you <em>really</em> want to use Hough Circles, youll want to get a much faster camera <em>and</em> have the hardware that can process &gt; 60 FPS.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=395832#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-395832&quot;, &quot;395832&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-397495"> 
              <p>I would suggest using <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2016/03/07/transparent-overlays-with-opencv/" rel="nofollow">transparent overlays</a>. You can blur the entire image using a smoothing method of your choice. This becomes your background. And then you can overlay the original, non-blurred object. This will require you to extract the ROI/mask of the object.</p>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-2"> <a name="comment-401541"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-401541" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">July 5, 2016 at 1:40 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-401541" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-401541"> 
              <p>You could certainly use a closing operation as well. In this case, I simply used a series of erosions and dilations. As for your second question, Im not sure what you mean.</p> 
              <p>The <em>fastest</em> tracking algorithm will undoubtedly be CAMShift. CAMShift is extremely fast since it only relies on the color histogram of an image. The Hough circle transform can be a bit slow, and worse, its a pain to tune the parameters. Haar cascades are very fast, but prone to false-positive detections. HOG is slower than Haar, but tends to be more accurate. If all you want to track is a green ball, then I would suggest using either the <code>cv2.inRange</code> function or CAMShift.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=401541#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-401541&quot;, &quot;401541&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

                  <p></p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-401765"> 
              <p>Sure, this is absolutely possible. It all comes down to how well you can detect the object/marker. If its easier to detect the person via color, do that. If the QR code gives you better detection accuracy, then go with that. I would suggest running a few tests and seeing what works best in your situation.</p>

            <p>Hi! Thanks for the tutorial! I have been learning OpenCV for a while now and I must say it is fascinating! I have an Arduino robot that I can control from my phone via bluetooth and it can also move around randomly while avoiding obstacles using a sonar range finder. Im in the process of adding a Raspberry Pi to the robot, which will detect a ball and instruct the Arduino to move toward it. Your tutorial has been very useful!</p> 
            <p>I was thinking of using houghcircles to check that the object is infact a ball but this proved a bit too difficult because of other stuff being picked up, or if I set the color range for the mask and the diameter for the circle too restrictively, the ball is not found because of, among other things, variations in the tone of color of the ball The robot should be able to detect the ball at some distance, so that brings certain requirements as well. I must say, I dont fully understand the Hough circle detection either, I often get a huge number of circles Maybe just detecting contours is enough for now.</p> 
            <p>Is it possible to detect the ball without resorting to color filtering?</p>

              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">July 18, 2016 at 5:25 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-402486" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-402486"> 
              <p>The parameters to Hough Circles can be a real pain to tune, so in general, I dont recommend using it. I would suggest instead filtering on your contour properties.</p> 
              <p>As for detecting a ball in an image <em>without</em> color filtering, thats absolutely possible. In general, you would need to <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/" rel="nofollow">train your own custom object detector</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=402486#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-402486&quot;, &quot;402486&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">August 10, 2016 at 9:30 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-404013" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-404013"> 
              <p>You can certainly track multiple objects at the same time. You just need to define the lower and upper color boundaries for each object you want to track. Then, generate a mask for each colored object and use the <code>cv2.findContours</code> function to find each of the objects.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=404013#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-404013&quot;, &quot;404013&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-404775"> 
              <p>To track the movement of the ball, <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/21/opencv-track-object-movement/" rel="nofollow">you can use this post</a>.</p> 
              <p>To track a different color object, be sure to use the <code>range-detector</code> script that I mention in the blog post. You can apply a square mask using <code>cv2.rectangle</code></p>

               <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-4"> <a name="comment-404891"></a> 
                <div id="li-comment-404891" class="comment-container"> 
                 <div class="avatar">
                  <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
                 </div> 
                 <div class="comment-head"> 
                  <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
                  <span class="date">August 24, 2016 at 3:51 pm</span> 
                  <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-404891" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
                  <span class="edit"></span> 
                 </div>
                 <!-- /.comment-head --> 
                 <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-404891"> 
                  <p>Basically, all you need to do is create two masks  one for the red and one for the green ball. Then, once you have these masks take the bitwise AND between them. This will give you any regions where the two colors overlap. You can find these regions using <code>cv2.findContours</code> or more simply <code>cv2.countNonZero</code></p> 
                  <div class="reply"> 
                   <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=404891#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-404891&quot;, &quot;404891&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
                  </div>

            <div id="li-comment-405327" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 1, 2016 at 10:55 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-405327" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-405327"> 
              <p>For multiple objects, I would suggest constructing a mask for each color. Once you have the masked regions for each color range, you can apply centroid tracking. Compute the Euclidean distance between your centroid objects between subsequent frames. Objects that have minimum distance should be associated and uniquely tracked together.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=405327#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-405327&quot;, &quot;405327&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-2"> <a name="comment-406023"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-406023" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 12, 2016 at 12:58 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-406023" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-406023"> 
              <p>Anytime you see an error related to NoneType, its because an image was not read properly from disk or (in this case) a frame was not read from a video stream. I would suggest going back to the <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/03/30/accessing-the-raspberry-pi-cameraats-with-opencv-and-python/" rel="nofollow">Accessing the Raspberry Pi camera post</a> and ensure that you can get the video stream working without any frame processing. From there, start to add in the code from this post in small bits.</p> 
              <p>Finally, if you need a jumpstart, I would suggest going through <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/practical-python-opencv/" rel="nofollow">Practical Python and OpenCV</a> to help you learn the basics of computer vision and OpenCV. All code examples in the book are compatible with the Raspberry Pi.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=406023#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-406023&quot;, &quot;406023&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <p>Hi Mostafa, I think you might have missed <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-359437" rel="nofollow">my reply to Nick above</a>. Given your inexperience with argparse, I think this is likely the issue though.              <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 21, 2016 at 2:16 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-406495" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-406495"> 
              <p>Its certainly possible to make the contrail larger or smaller based on the size of the ball. The larger the ball is, the closer we can assume it is to the camera. Similarly, the smaller the ball is, the farther away it is from the camera. Using this relationship you can adjust the size of contrail. The radius of the minimum enclosing circle at any given time will give you this information.</p> 
              <p>As for keeping <em>all</em> points of the contrail, simply sway out the <code>deque</code> for a standard Python list.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=406495#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-406495&quot;, &quot;406495&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-2"> <a name="comment-407309"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-407309" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">October 2, 2016 at 8:58 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-407309" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-407309"> 
              <p>Yes, the code certainly works for non-circular objects  this code assumes the largest region in the <code>mask</code> is the object you want to track. This could be circular or non-circular. If your object is non-circular you may want to compute the minimum bounding (rotated) rectangle versus the minimum enclosing circle. Other than that, nothing has to be changed.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=407309#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-407309&quot;, &quot;407309&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor even depth-2"> <a name="comment-408566"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-408566" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">October 20, 2016 at 8:42 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-408566" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-408566"> 
              <p>You can, but its not easy. You would require a high FPS camera since baseballs move extremely fast. If the camera is not a high FPS then youll have a lot of motion blur to deal with. In fact, <em>even with</em> a high FPS camera there will still be a lot of motion blur. Tracking motion of fast moving objects normally is a combination of image processing techniques + machine learning to actually predict where the ball is traveling.</p> 
              <p>I would suggest <a target="blank" href="http://baseball.physics.illinois.edu/TrackingBaseballs.pdf" rel="nofollow">starting with this paper</a> that reviews a ball tracking technique for pitches.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=408566#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-408566&quot;, &quot;408566&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <span class="date">November 4, 2016 at 10:02 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-409881" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-409881"> 
              <p>Tracking a player and a ball is a much more advanced project. I wouldnt recommend simple color thresholding for that. Instead, you should investigate correlation-based filters. These are much more advanced and even then being able to track a player across the pitch for an <em>entire</em> game is unrealistic. We can do it for short clips, but for not entire matches.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=409881#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-409881&quot;, &quot;409881&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <p>You can use <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/12/21/increasing-webcam-fps-with-python-and-opencv/" rel="nofollow">this blog post</a> to help you determine how many frames per second you are processing. Calls to <code>time.sleep</code> will allow you to properly set the number of frames per second that you want to process.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-410377"> 
              <p>Hey Mandy, while Im happy to provide free tutorials to help you learn about computer vision and image processing, I only support the Python code that I write. I do not provide support in converting code to other languages. I hope you understand.</p> 
              <div class="reply">

            <div id="li-comment-410680" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">November 14, 2016 at 12:04 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-410680" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-410680"> 
              <p>Hey Marlin  I would suggest using the HSV or L*a*b* color space as they are easier to define color ranges in. The problem will be lighting conditions. Consider a white object for instance. Under blue light the object will have a blue-ish tinge to it. Under direct light the white object will actually reflect the light. This makes it challenging to use color-based detection in varying lighting conditions.</p> 
              <p>In short, you <em>should</em> play around with varying HSV and L*a*b* values in your lighting conditions to determine what appropriate values are.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=410680#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-410680&quot;, &quot;410680&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-410677"> 
              <p>That really depends on the type of camera feed you are using. If the camera is fixed then simple background subtraction would suffice. If you are trying to work with moving cameras with lots of different lighting conditions then the problem becomes much harder. In general you will not find an out-of-the-box solution for this  youll likely need to code the solution yourself.</p>

             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-411040"> 
              <p>You need to define color thresholds for each of the balls. Loop over each of boundaries, color threshold the image, and compute contours. Instead of keeping only the largest contour, keep the contours that are sufficiently large.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=411040#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-411040&quot;, &quot;411040&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <p>Hey Kanta  are you using my example video included in the Downloads section of this post? If so (and youre not seeing an output video) then it sounds like your OpenCV installation was not compiled with video support. I would suggest <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/opencv-tutorials-resources-guides/" rel="nofollow">following one of my tutorials</a> on installing OpenCV on your system or using my pre-configured Ubuntu VirtualBox virtual machine included in <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/practical-python-opencv/" rel="nofollow">Practical Python and OpenCV</a>.</p>

              <span class="date">January 4, 2017 at 11:09 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-415134" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-415134"> 
              <p>The technique to do this really depends on how complex your image is. For basic images, thresholding and contour extraction is all you need. For more noisy images, you may need to apply a Hough Lines transform. For complex images, its entirely domain dependent.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=415134#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-415134&quot;, &quot;415134&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-415470"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-415470" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">January 9, 2017 at 9:10 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-415470" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-415470"> 
              <p>It sounds like youre in an environment where there are dramatic changes in lighting conditions. For example, the area of the room may be more bright close to your monitor and then as you pull the ball back the ball shifts into a darker region of the room.</p> 
              <p>Ideally, you should have uniform (or as close to as uniform) lighting conditions as possible to ensure your color thresholds work regardless of where the ball is. Its easier to write code that works for well-controlled environments that unconstrained ones.</p> 
              <p>If you cant change your lighting conditions, consider trying the L*a*b* color space or using multiple color thresholds. We use HSV/L*a*b* over RGB since it tends to be more intuitive to define colors in these color spaces and more representative of how humans perceive color.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=415470#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-415470&quot;, &quot;415470&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>
              <!-- /.reply -->

              <p>This will automatically install imutils for you.</p>

              <span class="date">January 24, 2017 at 2:23 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-416390" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-416390"> 
              <p>I admittedly have only used the NoIR camera once so I regrettably dont have much insight here. The problem here is that trying to detect and track light itself should be avoided. Think of how a camera captures an image  its actually capturing the light that <em>reflects</em> off the surfaces around it. This makes detecting <em>light itself</em> not advisable.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=416390#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-416390&quot;, &quot;416390&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

            <p> Your code perfectly works with arranging exact HSV range for an object thanks for this, but by varying lighting conditions HSV values of an object may significantly change, especially S and V values so it may detect other colors in different lighting conditions. You mentioned above about this problem and you said you need to find a solution yourself. </p>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-418245"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-418245" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">February 22, 2017 at 1:36 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-418245" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-418245"> 
              <p>If your lighting conditions are changing dramatically you may want to try the L*a*b* color space. It might also help if you can color calibrate your camera ahead of time. If thats not possible, you might want to consider machine learning based object detection. Depending on your objects, <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">HOG + Linear SVM</a> would be a good start.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=418245#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-418245&quot;, &quot;418245&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-418352"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-418352" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">February 24, 2017 at 11:27 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-418352" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-418352"> 
              <p>If you are getting a lot of tiny circles you might be detecting noise. Try applying a series or erosions and dilations to cleanup your mask.</p> 
              <p>You are also correct  if there are multiple objects with similar HSV ranges, they will be detected (this is a limitation of color-based object detection). In that case, you should try more structural object detection such as <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">HOG + Linear SVM</a>. I discuss this method in detail <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/pyimagesearch-gurus/">inside the PyImageSearch Gurus course</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=418352#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-418352&quot;, &quot;418352&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>
              <!-- /.reply --> 
             </div>
             <!-- /comment-entry --> 
            </div>
            <!-- /.comment-container --> </li>

You can run <code>pip freeze</code> to see which Python packages have been installed on your system, but this wont include the <code>cv2.so</code> file in the output. You can also <code>ls</code> the contents of your Pythons <code>site-packages</code> directory.</p>

              <span class="date">April 3, 2017 at 2:03 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-421850" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-421850"> 
              <p>If you are getting a <code>NoneType</code> error, its likely because your system is not properly decoding the frame. See <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2016/12/26/opencv-resolving-nonetype-errors/">this blog post</a> for more information on NoneType errors.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=421850#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-421850&quot;, &quot;421850&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">April 19, 2017 at 1:00 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-423239" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-423239"> 
              <p>If you want to use color to detect an object, then you would use the color thresholding technique mentioned in this blog post. Compute the centroid of object after color thresholding, then monitor the (x, y)-coordinates. If they change, youll know the object is moving.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=423239#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-423239&quot;, &quot;423239&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-423593"> 
              <p>Hi Sinjon  the <code>dequeue</code> data structure can store an object that you want (including a NumPy array). If would like to maintain a queue of the past N frames until some stopping criteria is met, just update the <code>dequeue</code> with the latest frames read from the camera.</p>

               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=423593#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-423593&quot;, &quot;423593&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-423576" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-423576"> 
              <p>Hey Marcos  you supply the video file path via command line argument when you start the script:</p> 
              <p><code>$ python ball_tracking.py --video ball_tracking_example.mp4</code></p> 
              <p>Notice how the <code>--video</code> switch points to a video file residing on disk.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-425404"> 
              <p>Hey Marcos  please see my reply to Ghanendra above related to tracking multiple objects. The gist is that you define color ranges for each type of object you want to detect and construct masks for each of them. If the objects are moving and there is a fixed, non-moving background <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/06/01/home-surveillance-and-motion-detection-with-the-raspberry-pi-python-and-opencv/">background subtraction</a> would be a better bet.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=425404#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-425404&quot;, &quot;425404&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">June 22, 2017 at 9:29 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-427870" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-427870"> 
              <p>The (x, y)-coordinates are stored in a <code>dequeue</code> object, as the code explains. To determine if a ball is moving forward, I would actually suggest monitoring the radius. As the radius increases, the ball is getting closer to the camera. As the radius decreases, the ball is moving farther away.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=427870#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-427870&quot;, &quot;427870&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-428260"> 
              <p>You certainly could train your own Haar cascade, although I would recommend the more accurate <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">HOG + Linear SVM detector</a>. I demonstrate how to build and implement the HOG + Linear SVM detector inside the <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/pyimagesearch-gurus/">PyImageSearch Gurus course</a>.</p>

             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">June 30, 2017 at 8:31 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-428592" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-428592"> 
              <p>That sounds quite tricky as there are a number of variables here. I would start by using a fixed camera in controlled lighting conditions. Color thresholding can be used to reveal the red vs. green color. As for ball tracking, that really depends on the type of ball. If the ball is colored, color thresholding could work. If the ball is a silver metallic, then color thresholding will not work due to reflections. You might need to train a custom <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">object objector</a> in that case.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=428592#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-428592&quot;, &quot;428592&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

              <p>This blog post was designed for OpenCV 2.4 and Python 2.7 (as there were no Python 3 bindings back then). Im assuming you are using Python 3 in which case you can change <code>xrange</code> to <code>range</code> and the code will work.</p>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-429844"> 
              <p>To start, I would suggest <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2016/01/04/unifying-picamera-and-cv2-videocapture-into-a-single-class-with-opencv/">using threading to increase your FPS processing rate</a>.</p> 
              <p>As for tracking, it depends on which algorithm you choose. Some tracking algorithms are fast, some very slow. If youre just getting started with computer vision you might want to use more standard laptop/desktop hardware to get a feel for various algorithms and compare performance on the Pi.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=429844#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-429844&quot;, &quot;429844&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-430102"> 
              <p>Hi Seth  yes, that is certainly possible. This method finds the largest object and tracks it; however, you could modify it to loop over all contours and simply discard those that are too small. Once you have detected the contours of the objects you can monitor their (x, y)-coordinates and check to see if they pass over a central line. From there, you would need to write code to communicate with your robot arm which is obviously device specific.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=430102#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-430102&quot;, &quot;430102&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a>

            <p>Hi Adrian,</p> 
            <p>First off, sweet website. Second, there must be at least two of you because you are just so on top of responding to all of the comments on this website. Anyway, I just wanted to make a comment regarding the range detector. </p> 
            <p>At first it was not working out for me. More specifically, I was not able to move the sliders that were controlling the threshold values or they would reset themselves and it was very difficult to terminate the script by pressing q. It seemed like python kept going through the while loop, which in turn was resetting my trackbars. Only pressing q at the right moment would allow me to stop the script. </p> 
            <p>I just added two more lines of code and now it works wonderfully. First, as you had suggested I inserted print(v1_min, v2_min, v3_min, v1_max, v2_max, v3_max) on line 103 within the if statement so the script would spit out some values. Secondly, I inserted cv.waitKey(0) as the final line of the while loop. </p> 
            <p>Im a total novice, so i dont know why it didnt work initially. Maybe it had something to do with my system? My operating system is MacOS Sierra (version 10.12.5) and I ran the script with python3.6.1 and the latest version of openCV.</p>

           <li class="comment byuser comment-author-adrian bypostauthor odd alt depth-2"> <a name="comment-435118"></a> 
            <div id="li-comment-435118" class="comment-container"> 
             <div class="avatar">
              <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=40&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/02743529311d3b8babbaf6935670ec9c?s=80&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-40 photo" height="40" width="40">
             </div> 
             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">September 18, 2017 at 2:08 pm</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-435118" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span> 
              <span class="edit"></span> 
             </div>
             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-435118"> 
              <p>Correct, when your lighting conditions change you cannot apply color thresholding-based techniques (as you the color threshold values will change). Instead you should consider applying a different object detection technique such as <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2014/11/10/histogram-oriented-gradients-object-detection/">HOG + Linear SVM</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=435118#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-435118&quot;, &quot;435118&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

             <div class="comment-head"> 
              <span class="name">Adrian Rosebrock</span> 
              <span class="date">October 2, 2017 at 9:56 am</span> 
              <span class="perma"><a href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/#comment-436250" title="Direct link to this comment">#</a></span>

             <!-- /.comment-head --> 
             <div class="comment-entry" id="comment-436250"> 
              <p>To start, your code is incorrect. You should be using <code>VideoStream</code> for both your USB camera and your Raspberry Pi camera module. For video files, use <code>FileVideoStream</code>.</p> 
              <p>Secondly, it sounds like Python cannot access your Raspberry Pi camera module. You can read up on common reasons for this in <a target="blank" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2016/08/29/common-errors-using-the-raspberry-pi-camera-module/">this post</a>.</p> 
              <div class="reply"> 
               <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://www.pyimagesearch.com/2015/09/14/ball-tracking-with-opencv/?replytocom=436250#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;comment-436250&quot;, &quot;436250&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;3051&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Adrian Rosebrock">Reply</a> 
              </div>

	var tag_cloud_height = jQuery( '#tagcloud').height();

	jQuery( '.inside ul li:last-child').css( 'border-bottom','0px' ); // remove last border-bottom from list in tab content
	jQuery( '.wooTabs').each(function(){

	});
	jQuery( '.inside > *').hide();
	jQuery( '.inside > *:first-child').show();

	jQuery( '.wooTabs li a').click(function(evt){ // Init Click funtion on Tabs

		var clicked_tab_ref = jQuery(this).attr( 'href' ); // Strore Href value

		jQuery(this).parent().parent().children( 'li').children( 'a').removeClass( 'selected' ); //Remove selected from all tabs

	})
